    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260502973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9709134008521820559"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429922357ra/14643839.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429922357ra/14643840.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429922357ra/14643841.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"She could walk into any hell and come back unscathed."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Rita. Vrataski. They call her crazy. They call her a badass. They call her a lot of names. <br/><br/>Angel of Death. Mad Wargarita. Full Metal Bitch. <br/><br/>Few know the truth. That she's all of those things. And more. And less. Even fewer know the reason why. Keiji Kiriya is about to join their ranks.<br/><br/>This is the story of two ordinary people forced to do the extraordinary; save the human race from an alien invasion. We meet Keiji, a green Japanese recrui</span>
  <span id="freeText9709134008521820559" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429922357ra/14643839.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429922357ra/14643840.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429922357ra/14643841.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"She could walk into any hell and come back unscathed."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Rita. Vrataski. They call her crazy. They call her a badass. They call her a lot of names. <br><br>Angel of Death. Mad Wargarita. Full Metal Bitch. <br><br>Few know the truth. That she's all of those things. And more. And less. Even fewer know the reason why. Keiji Kiriya is about to join their ranks.<br><br>This is the story of two ordinary people forced to do the extraordinary; save the human race from an alien invasion. We meet Keiji, a green Japanese recruit, on the day of his first battle. Nothing goes right. It's an ambush, a slaughter. The members of his unit are dropping like flies. Then he's fatally injured. <br><br>That's when he meets her. The crazy chick with the broadsword, her armor painted red to draw the enemy straight to her. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"The Full Metal Bitch.<br>I'd heard stories. A war junkie always chasing the action, no matter where it led her. Word had it she and her Special Forces squad from the U.S. Army had chalked up half of all confirmed Mimic kills ever. Maybe anyone who could see that much fighting and live to tell about it really was the Angel of Death."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Rita is one of the most badass characters I've ever encountered. I think my favorite thing about her is how understated she is. She doesn't run around pounding on her chest, aping masculine displays of dominance while declaring her badassery. Off the battlefield, she's just a regular, small town girl from the midwest. She's curious, a little gullible, and sweet. <br><br>And then she puts on an armor suit, heaves a broadsword, and rains down death and destruction from the mother fucking sky. <br><br>Keiji is not a badass. At least not in the beginning of this book. But then he kills a Mimic not quite like the others and inherits their strange ability to alter time, resetting it every time he dies. <br><br>He's also a regular guy. Actually, he's almost boringly ordinary in the beginning of this. Then he dies. Then he dies some more. Then he dies a lot more. And then he begins to change. He morphs from an average Japanese soldier into a Full Metal Mother Fucker. <br><br>This book is incredible. So much better than the movie <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Duh, right? Isn't that ALWAYS the case? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Less romance-heavy and more character study meets epic action sequences. And the writing, GAH, the writing. You feel every emotion. You hear every bomb drop: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I grip the trigger with stiff fingers: my arms shake as I send a rain of scorching steel down onto the enemy. The rifle kicks as I fire it. Vunk. Vunk. Vunk. A beat steadier than my heart. A soldier's spirit isn't in his body. It's in his weapon."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Now, if only I could kill me a Mimic and experience first time reading this over and over again. <br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9709134008521820559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/941225529?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=alternate-reality">alternate-reality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer941225529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16526525863921884564">I knew about this novel due that it's the basis for the incoming movie <i>Edge of Tomorrow</i> and I am truly glad that I was able to read the original Japanese novel before of watching the movie.<br/><br/>The novel itself is something odd in the Japanese literature culture, since it's a prose novel. I say this, since on Japan, the Manga culture is quite spread and even there are mangas for all tastes, genders and ages. And I must say that the topic and story of this novel could fit quite easily in a manga forma</span>
  <span id="freeText16526525863921884564" style="display:none">I knew about this novel due that it's the basis for the incoming movie <i>Edge of Tomorrow</i> and I am truly glad that I was able to read the original Japanese novel before of watching the movie.<br /><br />The novel itself is something odd in the Japanese literature culture, since it's a prose novel. I say this, since on Japan, the Manga culture is quite spread and even there are mangas for all tastes, genders and ages. And I must say that the topic and story of this novel could fit quite easily in a manga format presentation, since it's military sci-fi with cibernetic battle suits, involving time travel and an alien invasion. So, finding that the author chose to present this story in a prose novel was something quite brave.<br /><br />I just found out that it will be a manga adaptation of the story, most likely since the prose novel got a lot of hype due the incoming live action movie. I am a huge fan of manga, but I am truly glad of being able to read first the story on its original format.<br /><br />To explain quick what you can expect here, it's like <i>Groundhog Day</i> meets <i>Halo</i>.<br /><br />I really like how smart is this novel. It presents a great characters' development. Also it's a festival of genres, while the military science-fiction is the main genre, you can find too elements of dystopia, mystery, politics and romance. Also, the author did a great work establishing his own sci-fi technology, how it works and how the pilots must use it. Everything in a total adult way.<br /><br />The main characters are Keiji Kiriya and Rita Vrataski. Something quite amusing when the characters are described is that Rita Vrataski is a petite woman with red hair, but due she is a hero of the army forces, it will be done a movie on U.S. about her, and it's said that the chosen actress is a tall blonde woman, that it's how Emily Blunt will performed the character on the incoming movie.<br /><br />The interaction between the main characters and the interaction of them with the secondary characters, everything is done masterfully with realism and depth.<br /><br /><b>HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!!!</b><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16526525863921884564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_637876788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637876788" />
    <a title="Jokoloyo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1902630-jokoloyo"><img alt="Jokoloyo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423473158p2/1902630.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637876788?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jokoloyo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jokoloyo" href="/user/show/1902630-jokoloyo">Jokoloyo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jokoloyo by: </span>
      apple
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637876788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9393425315118565387">I love <i> Groundhog Day</i> movie, especially how the character grew from hopeless person into a great character that proficient using the time loops. so, when I realized the premise in this book is time looping mixed with military SF, I am sold. <br/><br/>When Apple, my GR friend, recommended me this book, I have never heard about Japanese light novel format. (Later I learned that It was basically another name of shorter novel, or novella). So it was an exotic recommendation: a fiction from a Japanese author, </span>
  <span id="freeText9393425315118565387" style="display:none">I love <i> Groundhog Day</i> movie, especially how the character grew from hopeless person into a great character that proficient using the time loops. so, when I realized the premise in this book is time looping mixed with military SF, I am sold. <br /><br />When Apple, my GR friend, recommended me this book, I have never heard about Japanese light novel format. (Later I learned that It was basically another name of shorter novel, or novella). So it was an exotic recommendation: a fiction from a Japanese author, a SF story mixing military and time-loop, in unfamiliar format.<br /><br />From the start, the story is an easy 4 star rating, with a lot of action scenes and the character developments. But when I was reading the table of contents, I was struck. <br />1. The timeline of the story is not linear, and there is flowchart explaining the timeline of the story. The author is serious in making non linear story and I admit the flowchart is effective to making the reading experience more enjoyable.<br />2. The book is divided into four parts. The book structure is reminding me of a japanese poem. I read a poem at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jeffinous.blogspot.com/2011/12/japanese-koan.html">http://jeffinous.blogspot.com/2011/12...</a> which is:<br /><br />Two sisters of a Kyoto silk merchant, pretty as flowers,<br />One aged twenty, the other eighteen.<br />Swords of militia can kill multitudes of life,<br />Seductive glances from these two beauties can slay entire armies.<br /><br />I had high expectation reading this book. After I finished it, I am satisfied because this book fulfilled my expectation. I was expecting the book was divided into four-part. Just like the poem above; the first line contains the initial phrase; the second line, the continuation of that phrase; the third line turns from this subject and begins a new one; and the fourth line brings the first three lines together. <br /><br />Oh, I risk indirect spoilers just by quoting the poem. :P <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The first and second part are the story from POV of Kiriya. The third part has POV from Rita Vrataski. The fourth part is where two protagonists join forces. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />As if I ordered the book written according to my own criteria. An unexpected excellent reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9393425315118565387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2830130092?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly">Beverly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68708752-beverly?shelf=science-fiction-thriller">science-fiction-thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2830130092&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2830130092" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1998234019875668717">Aliens combat an Earth force made up of Japanese, American and other nations in All You Need is Kill. The Japanese soldier is caught in a Groundhog Day nightmare of kill, be killed, sleep, and repeat. He doesn't know what is happening to him until he meets an American soldier who is also caught in a time loop.Together they can defeat the aliens, but they have to solve the puzzle in time. A quick read with an interesting premise.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_958921460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/958921460" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/958921460?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12868204-all-you-need-is-kill">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carmen by: </span>
      Movie
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=he-says">he-says</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=published2014">published2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=japanese-author">japanese-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer958921460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15581560393931736394">War is hell.<br/><br/>The Mimics and the humans have been fighting for decades now, with no end in sight. Relentless, innumerable, and nearly unstoppable, the Mimics keep coming in waves. They've turned most of the world into a desert and killed millions of people.<br/><br/>Keiji Kiriya is just a grunt. The woman he loves, a sweet librarian, won't even look him in the eye, and the way things are now the army seems like his only viable option. Training has turned him into a hard-bodied soldier, but when it comes to </span>
  <span id="freeText15581560393931736394" style="display:none">War is hell.<br /><br />The Mimics and the humans have been fighting for decades now, with no end in sight. Relentless, innumerable, and nearly unstoppable, the Mimics keep coming in waves. They've turned most of the world into a desert and killed millions of people.<br /><br />Keiji Kiriya is just a grunt. The woman he loves, a sweet librarian, won't even look him in the eye, and the way things are now the army seems like his only viable option. Training has turned him into a hard-bodied soldier, but when it comes to battle he's just cannon fodder.<br /><br />Rita Vratraski is the Full Metal Bitch. U.S. Special Forces - she is the best of the best. She has won so many medals she had to take out a storage facility. But medals don't matter to her. She isolates herself from the rest of the soldiers, and insists on wearing a blood-red Jacket - even though this makes her an attractive target for the Mimics. She slices through them as if she was born to kill. She's a legend. The men talk about her in hushed whispers, and even a glimpse of her on the battlefield boosts morale. She's slaughtered thousands of Mimics, and refuses to use the weapons the army provides - instead she wields a huge battleaxe twice her size.<br /><br />One day, during battle, Keiji kills a Mimic that he feels is...a bit different. He doesn't know how he knows this...he just does. And after he dies a gruesome death on the battlefield...he wakes up in bed two days ago.<br /><br />Keiji tries many different things to get out of the time loop. Running away, wounding himself, and eating a bullet. Nothing works. He's damned to live this day over and over and over again.<br /><br />So he figures he'd better make the best of a bad situation. He starts training, hardcore. One day of training, one day of battle... and then it's back to training day again. He relives these two days over and over hundreds of times, until even though technically he's still a grunt with no battle experience, he's got the skills and reflexes of a grizzled veteran. He's turned himself into Billy Badass.<br /><br />He sweet-talks the cute, naïve, clumsy engineer into given him a battleaxe like the one that the Full Metal Bitch carries. He starts carving holes in enemy lines.<br /><br />Then one loop, he and the Full Metal Bitch get to talking...and from then on she's just Rita. <br /><br />Together, they form an unstoppable team, perfectly attuned to each other as if they'd fought in countless battles together.<br /><br />And of course, they have.<br /><br />This is a heartrending, powerful story that I never expected to like. I only read it to prepare for the upcoming movie. (They re-named it EDGE OF TOMORROW for some reason - I infinitely prefer ALL YOU NEED IS KILL, but okay). I never expected to like a war novel written by a man who's played one too many videogames.<br /><br />I liked Keiji. He could've easily and justifiably been a real a**hole, but instead he's almost a pacifist, never responding to a fight (from a fellow soldier). He also treats women well, I think. There were numerous times when he could've really taken advantage of a situation with a female, and he never did. I know it's stupid to give men credit for NOT doing something horrifying, but I'm disgusted with the recent onslaught of a**hole "heroes" who treat women like trash. I appreciated a bit of restraint and respect on the part of Keiji.<br /><br />I loved the style that this book was written in. See my status updates if you want samples. Crisp, clear, to the point - exactly my kind of writing. No flowery prose. No long descriptions. No inundation of adjectives. I have no idea whether to credit Sakurazaka for this or credit the Japanese-English translation. I mention this because I really adore the writing style (if not the content) of Swedish and Norwegian books - it doesn't seem to matter who writes them. This leads me to believe that translating into English lends a clear, concise voice to these works. I don't have the same vast experience with Japanese-to-English translations, so the jury's still out. It's only a theory at this point.<br /><br />I also was pleasantly surprised that Sakurazaka takes the time and energy to show us how Rita sees things, and how she came to be the Full Metal Bitch. I really was expecting this book to be only from Keiji's viewpoint (3rd person viewpoint) and I appreciate that Sakurazaka takes the more difficult route in trying to create three-dimensional characters. Well done.<br /><br />Lastly, I didn't feel like he pushed the sex/sex appeal/sexy situation angle too hard. It would have been very, very easy to make this book full of questionable sexual content, but Sakurazaka plays it pretty straightforward. I'm very thankful for that.<br /><br />Tl;dr - a thrilling and worthwhile read, whether you plan on seeing the film or not. I thoroughly enjoyed every minute of it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15581560393931736394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_761238519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761238519" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761238519?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761238519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4625020326650967131"><i>As a kid, when I’d first laid eyes on those guns, I thought they were the coolest things I’d ever seen.<br/>The black lacquer finish of their steel instilled an unreasonable sense of confidence in me. Now that I’d seen real battle, I knew with cool certainty that weapons like these could never repel a Mimic attack.</i><br/><br/>I’ve had my eye on <i>All You Need is Kill</i> for some time now. When I saw that the book is being adapted into a film, I thought that now is as good a time as any to read it. And I’m glad I did,</span>
  <span id="freeText4625020326650967131" style="display:none"><i>As a kid, when I’d first laid eyes on those guns, I thought they were the coolest things I’d ever seen.<br />The black lacquer finish of their steel instilled an unreasonable sense of confidence in me. Now that I’d seen real battle, I knew with cool certainty that weapons like these could never repel a Mimic attack.</i><br /><br />I’ve had my eye on <i>All You Need is Kill</i> for some time now. When I saw that the book is being adapted into a film, I thought that now is as good a time as any to read it. And I’m glad I did, too.<br /><br />The beauty of Science Fiction is that there is so much a talented author can do with it. This novel is a case in point. <i>All You Need is Kill</i> is a Military Science Fiction story, complete with power armour and malicious Aliens. However…<br /><br /><i>Attempt #99:<br />KIA forty-five minutes from start of battle.</i><br /><br />…the novel has a <b>great</b> hook. Perhaps things are not quite what they seem. In some respects <i>All You Need is Kill</i> shares DNA with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/102327.Armor" title="Armor by John Steakley" rel="nofollow noopener">Armor</a>, especially the converging story lines of Kiriya and the Full Metal Bitch.<br /> <br /><i>Genocide was the only way to win this war.</i><br /><br />The writing style can be a bit jarring. This could be a side-effect of the translation from Japanese, or perhaps not, since it actually complements the general feel of the novel quite well.<br /><br />And that is that. Really not more to say.<br /><br /><i>The fear that permeated every fiber of my being was relentless, it was cruel, and it was my best hope for getting through this.</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4625020326650967131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2767683114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2767683114" />
    <a title="Ken" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38999260-ken"><img alt="Ken" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446483502p2/38999260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2767683114?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken" href="/user/show/38999260-ken">Ken</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2767683114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17944789716857359886">I’ve only recently found out that the 2014 fun action adventure movie ‘Edge of Tomorrow’ was based on this 2004 Japanese Sci-Fi light read.<br/><br/>Young recruit Keiji Kiriya soon discovers that he’s caught in a time loop against the alien ‘Mimics’, after each death he awakes on the eve of battle and attempts to progress future with the knowledge he’s previously learnt from the last loop.<br/><br/>It’s been so long since I’d watched the Cruise movie adaptation, but I felt that even though the basic premise was sim</span>
  <span id="freeText17944789716857359886" style="display:none">I’ve only recently found out that the 2014 fun action adventure movie ‘Edge of Tomorrow’ was based on this 2004 Japanese Sci-Fi light read.<br /><br />Young recruit Keiji Kiriya soon discovers that he’s caught in a time loop against the alien ‘Mimics’, after each death he awakes on the eve of battle and attempts to progress future with the knowledge he’s previously learnt from the last loop.<br /><br />It’s been so long since I’d watched the Cruise movie adaptation, but I felt that even though the basic premise was similar this felt more character driven.<br /><br />I really like this kind of story telling and it’s becoming more common place along with Happy Death Day and Russian Dolls, I love the Sci-Fi elements of these Groundhog Day style stories.<br /><br />I can really appreciate the fact that this book has helped spurn that genre.<br />It’s so distinctive and different which is mainly due to the great characters, that those who like similar stories should also read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17944789716857359886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_525000436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/525000436" />
    <a title="Haralambi Markov " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233458-haralambi-markov"><img alt="Haralambi Markov " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359878879p2/1233458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/525000436?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haralambi Markov " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haralambi Markov " href="/user/show/1233458-haralambi-markov">Haralambi Markov </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233458-haralambi-markov?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer525000436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1729423403025109034">I had a very hard time starting this review. There is much to say and reflect upon, yet “All You Need is Kill” is unlike most novels the American and the European audience has had experience with. Prose, length, storytelling, characterization, internals and general take on the genre; all these elements create unfamiliar alien scenery, which needs discovering and an adventurous spirit to experiment with the unknown.<br/><br/>Science fiction is as wide as the universe it explores, virtually endless and whil</span>
  <span id="freeText1729423403025109034" style="display:none">I had a very hard time starting this review. There is much to say and reflect upon, yet “All You Need is Kill” is unlike most novels the American and the European audience has had experience with. Prose, length, storytelling, characterization, internals and general take on the genre; all these elements create unfamiliar alien scenery, which needs discovering and an adventurous spirit to experiment with the unknown.<br /><br />Science fiction is as wide as the universe it explores, virtually endless and while the Western culture has taken up the undying space exploration themes, colonization and the such, the Eastern have adopted the apocalypse by aliens/humans and made it their own. Try an anime and you will see what I am talking about. “All You Need is Kill” portrays the final stand of humanity against an invading alien force, devoted to turning Earth into a colony. In a sense this is military fiction, but it doesn’t get boring or falls into cliché.<br /><br />The Japanese are known for their brevity in literature, mostly with the worldwide celebrated haikus, but their sense to get down to the point and write the distilled and concentrated essence of their topic crosses into speculative fiction. Sakurazaka builds his novel more around the internals of the characters and how they process the occurrences in their life much like a report. Compared to what we are used in the West dialogue is overall scarce and actual combat scenes are also few in number, but Sakurazaka creates the illusion that writing war and combat scenes is like the easiest thing in the world.<br /><br />Despite its 169 pages by Hiroshi offers a full novel experience much like any title ranging from 300 to 600 pages. This proves to show that length in literature is quite subjective and the page count steps down in importance to the use of words, which combination will reduce an idea or image to one concise power pack to the reader.<br /><br />Characters &amp; Depth: Remarkable in “All You Need is Kill” is the rapid character evolution. Keiji on page one is a rookie with no battle experience and meets his death in a cowardly manner, while Keiji from the last chapter is a veteran with steel nerves and body turned into a killing machine. This metamorphosis once you have invested all your enthusiasm in the story is invisible so to say. You pick up a change, but it is so natural given the situation that he is in a time loop and every day is a struggle to end it. But once you stop to think about it you get the wow effect. At least I have. This wouldn’t have worked, if the novel itself was longer.<br /><br />The story is told in third person POV and changes from Keiji to Rita aka the Full Metal Bitch, who has become a legendary soldier, because a time loop herself. Her role in the novel is quite interesting and dramatic following the guidelines of Japanese sense of tragedy. She highlights the events that occur in the time loop through her own experience, which gives credible explanation to the constant resurrection of Keiji. Being a tough person in the present, by the same rules we are introduced to her own personal anguish and shattered existence. In the end Keiji and Rita represent two aspects of the super soldier, Keiji is the process of hardening yourself and carrying an unimaginable burden, while Rita is the broken person left in the process. There is this yin-yang polarity so to say. <br /><br />Worldbuilding &amp; Believability: I wasn’t a great fan in the beginning, when I found out this whole book will revolve over a battle that repeats itself around 160 times. I have seen the idea done before in the show “Tru Calling” and in some movies I don’t remember very clearly, so I wasn’t charmed. But then again the focus came on the internal development of the character and how he tries everything to stop waking up every day on the same date before the same battle. If you view it gamer terms, it’s having to reset the same level 160 times and every time gain new experience after failing, try new strategy and develop mad skills.<br /><br />The Mimics are the core of the very problem. In the book they are described as dead bloated frogs and are basically made out of nanobots and have evolved from a remodeling tool for colonization to weapons. They even have the technology to reset time and are the culprits for the constant time loops. I won’t say more, because the whole situation is definitely more complex than that and offers twists and thrill rides that leave you “awesome”-ing all the while.<br /><br />Perhaps the last element in the whole world now that we mentioned the aliens and time loops is the so called Jackets. They are your simple full battle armor with major artillery and a constant in the whole novel, plus they create this whole subculture in the army with special training system, slang and all that to make it interesting. <br /><br />The Verdict: I love it and advise people to give it a chance. Speaking from a globalization point of view, now more than ever we have the ultimate freedom to touch another culture and explore it. So take a chance and see how the other side of the world does it. You know you want to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1729423403025109034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1970801966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1970801966" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1970801966?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421560878" href="/book/show/17571487-edge-of-tomorrow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970801966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16267570501130755727">For some reason this Tom Cruise movie was a blockbuster bust, but it was because of the excellent movie that I wanted to delve into this concept a bit more. After picking up the book, it's clear almost immediately that the film whitewashed the book and that destroys one of the very simple yet profound themes of this book, which I'll get to in a sec.<br/><br/>Keiji Kiriya is a simple Japanese soldier who finds himself in a time loop, experiencing the same couple days and deaths over and over only to wake u</span>
  <span id="freeText16267570501130755727" style="display:none">For some reason this Tom Cruise movie was a blockbuster bust, but it was because of the excellent movie that I wanted to delve into this concept a bit more. After picking up the book, it's clear almost immediately that the film whitewashed the book and that destroys one of the very simple yet profound themes of this book, which I'll get to in a sec.<br /><br />Keiji Kiriya is a simple Japanese soldier who finds himself in a time loop, experiencing the same couple days and deaths over and over only to wake up in the barracks once more and experience it all again. The war he's in is against an alien race named the "mimics" who are all but unstoppable, until humanity created mechanized suits, "jackets," to be able to deal with them.<br /><br />And that's pretty simply it. There's some slight exposition about the aliens and the future this world finds itself in, however, it's mostly focused on Keiji and his time loops. <br /><br />I don't want to spoil anything too much so I'll give this warning first. In an afterword, the author, Hiroshi Sakurazaka, explains that he got the idea for this book from playing video games. You respawn so much throughout the game, you get really good at it. You also get really good at seeing the things that will be coming at you. In the end of the video game, you're praised as a hero, but really you're just an average Joe who had endless amounts of retries so you ended up getting good!<br /><br />And that's the brilliance of the book. There are no superpowers, unless you count the futuristic jackets and accompanying weapons. It's just an average guy, a novice even, who finds himself in a really crappy Groundhog Day scenario (at least Bill Murray's deaths were of his own volition), and decides to make the best of it by trying to get better every time.<br /><br />Great concept both in book and movie form and the book's different enough from the movie (or vice versa) to make it worth reading, especially given the 266 pages mmpb. The only real problem is I want more.<br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (highly recommended)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16267570501130755727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_849100582" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/849100582" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/849100582?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=action-challenge-3">action-challenge-3</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=scifi-fan-challenge-2014">scifi-fan-challenge-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=gritty-reads">gritty-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=new-sci-fi-fantasy-authors-challeng">new-sci-fi-fantasy-authors-challeng</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=books-to-films-challenge-3-2014">books-to-films-challenge-3-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer849100582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18065524498857248421"><i>
  <blockquote>"That's the thing with books. Half the time the author doesn't know what the hell he's writing about - especially not those war novelists."</blockquote>
</i> <br/><br/><i>All You Need Is Kill</i> is a military science fiction novel by Hiroshi Sakurazaka and which follows the tradition of western science fiction works such as <i>The Forever War</i> by Joe Halderman. However, <i>All You Need Is Kill</i> has its own blend of adrenaline and fury that works to convey the themes of the novel wonderfully, even as a translation. That is the mark o</span>
  <span id="freeText18065524498857248421" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"That's the thing with books. Half the time the author doesn't know what the hell he's writing about - especially not those war novelists."</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br /><i>All You Need Is Kill</i> is a military science fiction novel by Hiroshi Sakurazaka and which follows the tradition of western science fiction works such as <i>The Forever War</i> by Joe Halderman. However, <i>All You Need Is Kill</i> has its own blend of adrenaline and fury that works to convey the themes of the novel wonderfully, even as a translation. That is the mark of a strong science fiction novel: when the themes are conveyed even when translated. <br /><br /><i>All You Need Is Kill</i> is about to be released as the Tom Cruise film <i>Edge of Tomorrow</i> (with some changes likely to be made to the source material). It was for this reason that I was interested in checking out the novel and seeing what type of book it was. The novel itself features the ideas of time-travel, mech-suits (as with Robert Heinlein's classic <i>Starship Troopers</i>), advanced weaponry and aliens. There are two heroes to this tale if you will, though the main protagonist is Keiji Kiriya, a warrior engaged in a battle against half biological, half mechanical alien warriors called Mimics, for the survival of humanity. During one of these battles he encounters the legendary warrior known privately as the Mad Wargarita (among other names) and dies. Only to reawaken the morning before the battle even began.<br /><br />As it turns out our hero is caught in a loop reminiscent of the old Bill Murray movie <i>Groundhog Day</i>. This cycle of death and rebirth becomes a cycle which allows Keiji to learn and learn and learn, death after death after death. I don't quite consider this a spoiler, firstly because these details can be read on the jacket of the book and secondly because the real details of the novel is found in the way in which Keiji and the female warrior engage with each other as they discover and rediscover each other across this loop. The people in the novel are always the same and yet slightly different: which poses the interesting meta-question 'Are humans changed subtly by their possession of different types of knowledge and by our experiences?'<br /><br />Of course this book is about far more than simply identity and how our choices and actions define us. As much as it is a science fiction ride it is also a war novel: a novel that confronts how war affects everyone and reshapes every soldier into a machine. At one point Keiji reflects upon the scariness of the Mimics in that they do not inspire primal fear like eagles screeching or bears growling and standing on hind feet. They create fear by being calculating and predatory at the same time. This I think, is what the true horror of modern war is: that it becomes a cold, calculating game of numbers and attrition. In this remark this 'loopy' future (pardon the pun) that Sakurazaka describes is a future not so dissimilar from out own. Minus the alien killing machines.<br /><br />I used the quote at the beginning of this review because I wanted to highlight the subtly written humour of the novel. It is a novel full of its own in-jokes linked to other aspects of science fiction and in many ways I suppose the particular quote I highlight is a kind of meta-joke. In its own right I suspect one could read this entire book as a meta-joke about science fiction. A work questioning all the possibilities of what can happen across one day if subtle things change every so often. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18065524498857248421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1263572890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263572890" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263572890?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263572890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11807506101125824496">So what do you get when you mix Groundhog Day, a war manga, and Tony Stark's suit of armor he made in a cave? You get All You Need Is Kill. Keiji Kiriya is stuck in a loop fighting aliens to the death...well to his death. Keiji has died during each of his 158 tries to get out of the loop. <i>Bill Murray's character in Groundhog Day had it way easier than Keiji Kiriya.</i><br/><br/>For me All You Need Is Kill is a book with an interesting concept that falls short once Rita Vrataski gets her own point of view. I d</span>
  <span id="freeText11807506101125824496" style="display:none">So what do you get when you mix Groundhog Day, a war manga, and Tony Stark's suit of armor he made in a cave? You get All You Need Is Kill. Keiji Kiriya is stuck in a loop fighting aliens to the death...well to his death. Keiji has died during each of his 158 tries to get out of the loop. <i>Bill Murray's character in Groundhog Day had it way easier than Keiji Kiriya.</i><br /><br />For me All You Need Is Kill is a book with an interesting concept that falls short once Rita Vrataski gets her own point of view. I don't want to spoil anything so I won't explain any more then saying the author should've never tried to explain how the loops work. Perhaps that isn't fair, the best way to say it is don't explain something you don't fully understand. Time travel scenarios can be as messy and annoying as stepping in poop and tracking it all around your home. Let's just say the author was likely walking around a farm with serious nasal congestion before he headed home.<br /><br />The story itself was intriguing prior to the Vrataski info dump. Poor Keiji has walked into a reasonable facsimile of hell. After the inevitable attempts to run away and commit suicide to escape the loops, Keiji decides to train his mind to help him win the battle. This part was enjoyable to see how he had learned to navigate his day and the battle with the proficient ease of 100 plus attempts.<br /><br />All I Need Is Kill felt like a case of unfulfilled potential. Perhaps I'll have to watch the movie to find out if they did a better job utilizing the concept.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11807506101125824496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1260244463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1260244463" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260244463?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=all-the-feels">all-the-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=amazing-characters">amazing-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=badassery">badassery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260244463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14237648756400416496">War. Terrible war. Humans vs a race of aliens called Mimics. It's been going on for years now and it seems to go forever - with the odds for humanity growing slimmer with each day that passes. This is the world in which Keiji Kiriya, a Japanese recruit, lives.<br/><br/>Today is gonna be his first battle, and to make him feel even worse, he gets injured.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>I'm gonna die on a fucking battlefield. On some godforsaken island with no friends, no family, no girlfriend. In pain, in fear, covered in my own shit b</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14237648756400416496" style="display:none">War. Terrible war. Humans vs a race of aliens called Mimics. It's been going on for years now and it seems to go forever - with the odds for humanity growing slimmer with each day that passes. This is the world in which Keiji Kiriya, a Japanese recruit, lives.<br><br>Today is gonna be his first battle, and to make him feel even worse, he gets injured.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I'm gonna die on a fucking battlefield. On some godforsaken island with no friends, no family, no girlfriend. In pain, in fear, covered in my own shit because of the fear. And I can't even raise the only weapon I have left to fend off the bastard racing toward me. It was like all the fire in me left with my last round of ammo.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>That's when he meets Rita Vrataski, the Full Metal Bitch.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I’d heard stories. A war junkie always chasing the action, no matter where it led her. Word had it she and her Special Forces squad from the U.S. Army had chalked up half of all confirmed Mimic kills ever. Maybe anyone who could see that much fighting and live to tell about it really was the Angel of Death.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>She's the most famous soldier of the war. Her abilities in killing Mimics cannot be outstanded by anyone. Too bad the odds were not with Keiji that day, because in the end he died... only to wake up the day before his battle and feel as if all had been a dream.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I remembered the whole thing. I was nervous about it being my first battle, so I’d decided to duck out a bit early. I had come back to my bunk and started reading that mystery novel. I even remembered helping Yonabaru up to his bed when he came staggering in from partying with the ladies.<br><br>Unless—unless I had dreamed that too?</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Again he goes to war and dies and wakes up in the same way he did the previous time. Over and over again.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>So long as the wind blows, I’m born again, and I die. I can’t take anything with me to my next life. The only things I get to keep are my solitude, a fear that no one can understand, and the feel of<br>the trigger against my finger.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Rita Vrataski and Keiji Kiriya may easily be one of the best cast of characters I've read about. None of them is perfect. Keiji is not fearless, for example. He's terrified of death and he's not afraid of telling you that. He also feels alone quite most of the time, and things have never gone the way he plans. He had motives of his own for enlisting in the army.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429939544ra/14646112.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked being inside his head. His narration was easy to follow and it was highly enjoyable. It was funny at some points and I connected with him very fast, which is something that influences a lot in my rating for a book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I was weak. I couldn’t even get the woman I loved—the librarian—to look me in the eye.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I also loved how he grows as a character throughout the book. At the beginning he is no other than a normal guy you could find on the streets, but once he grabs hold of his “ability”, he starts training to become the soldier he dreams to be.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Pretending to be a hero slain in battle was one thing. Dying a hero in a real war was another. As I got older, I understood the difference, and I knew I didn’t wanna die. Not even in a dream.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The other character I mentioned, Rita, was by far my favorite, though.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The Americans called Rita the Full Metal Bitch, or sometimes just Queen Bitch. When no one was listening, we called her Mad Wargarita.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429919071ra/14643531.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Right now, I can't remember the last time I read about such a kick-ass character. She's strong, brave, she doesn't like people messing with her and she hates Mimics with all her soul. Like, she has a very personal reason to hate them.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>If she had a bad headache, she’d go apeshit, killing friend and foe alike. And yet not a single enemy round had ever so much as grazed her Jacket. She could walk into any hell and come back unscathed.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Her backstory has just as amazing as herself too. And she's a well developed character as well. I feel like there should be more books with these kind of characters: Strong, badass and confident. And even when she has all those things, she's just a normal girl – no special snowflake.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Rita’s only other distinguishing feature was the red hair she’d inherited from her grandmother. Everything else about her was exactly like any other of over three hundred million Americans.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And don't even get me started on the writing... “Full Amazing Writing” would be the perfect words to describe it. You can feel everything. Full load of feels all over the way. Some times I couldn't help but laugh out loud, some others made me a little sad, others kept me at the edge of my seat because the action was very intense. In summary, I <i>felt</i>, which you already know is something I consider important while reading a book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>You can’t learn from your mistakes when they kill you. These greenhorns didn’t know what it was to walk the razor’s edge between life and death. They didn’t know that the line dividing the two, the borderland piled high with corpses, was the easiest place to survive. The fear that permeated every fiber of my being as relentless, it was cruel, and it was my best hope for getting through this.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>My only complaint for this book is that it didn't last longer. Really, I started it at 3 pm this day and I ended it at 10:30 pm. I finished it in 7 effing hours! Never could I stop myself from reading it. Now I just wish to go back and read it again, for entertainment's sake and because it also had some really awesome quotes I'd like to re-read.<br><br>Truly recommended.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14237648756400416496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2871293995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2871293995" />
    <a title="Allison Hurd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd"><img alt="Allison Hurd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530670583p2/14495279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2871293995?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Hurd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Hurd" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd">Allison Hurd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=authors-of-color">authors-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=man-author">man-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-2019-challenge">sff-2019-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-bookshelf">sff-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871293995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2406768061369509375">Perhaps I'm doing a bit of the heavy lifting here, but I thought this was a searing, sardonic look at the atrocity of war and the horror of PTSD. Also there were mech suits, kaiju aliens, and battle glaives!<br/><br/><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: (no actual spoilers, just a list of topics) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ graphic violence, war, racism, depiction of mental illness, loss of a loved one.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><u>Things to love:</u><br/><br/>-<b>The tone</b>. This translation was excellent. It read seamlessly, and got a lot of humor and sarcasm in the</span>
  <span id="freeText2406768061369509375" style="display:none">Perhaps I'm doing a bit of the heavy lifting here, but I thought this was a searing, sardonic look at the atrocity of war and the horror of PTSD. Also there were mech suits, kaiju aliens, and battle glaives!<br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: (no actual spoilers, just a list of topics) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ graphic violence, war, racism, depiction of mental illness, loss of a loved one.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Things to love:</u><br /><br />-<b>The tone</b>. This translation was excellent. It read seamlessly, and got a lot of humor and sarcasm in there to boot, which is the hardest thing to translate in a way that feels natural. I thought this book nailed it. I was shocked and over my head, I was confused, I was angry, determined, desperate, hopeful and doomed at intervals. And throughout there was this sort of Catch-22-esque undercurrent that this is both tragically futile and dangerously funny.<br /><br />-<b>The characters</b>. Rita, the sergeant, the mechanic (sorry, I listened to the audiobook and names aren't my strong suit) were all very interesting. I liked seeing a Japanese take on stereotypes and positive characteristics. It was just "not western" enough that I had things to think about during more predictable plot points.<br /><br />-<b>The imagery</b>. Friends, this is about a very unstable dude in a mech suit with a battle axe, and his even more badass battle-axe wielding lady friend. That's just fun. But aside from that, a lot of the aliens, futuristic elements and the world we glimpse is startling and full of implications.<br /><br />-<b>Examination of the trauma of war</b>. For the vast majority of the book this felt like the story of someone trying to cope with PTSD, and I thought it was told in a way that resonated with a lot of my knowledge on the topic. It felt bleak but also had a "well, what else are you going to do?" sense to it that felt very honest to people struggling with mental health issues. It wasn't an easy thing to read, but I thought it handled that well.<br /><br /><u>Things that weren't the best</u> (caution, some spoilers--headings are safe):<br /><br />-<b>Plot familiarity</b>. It's Groundhog Day meets Catch-22 with mech suits. You know how this story is going to go.<br /><br />-<b>Overlong battles</b>. The battles weren't the interesting part. As with all stories of this ilk, the psychology of the person stuck in time is what's fascinating. I thought the battles were well-described, but they weren't really what I was here for, after the first few kills so that I could enjoy the battle axe mech component.<br /><br />-<b>The ending</b>. This was the only point that I'm not sure the translation was perfect. The end came on a bit abruptly and I'm not sure how or why this was what their solution had to be. It also kind of shattered the allegory I had going on (real spoiler) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that Keijei was experiencing trauma that kept him locked forever in his head <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which was one of the things I enjoyed about the ongoing story. <br /><br />A 3.5 star read rounded up because I was pleasantly surprised and would recommend this to others who like these types of stories. I also can recommend the audiobook, which I thought was well performed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2406768061369509375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2860626223" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2860626223" />
    <a title="Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony"><img alt="Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534088626p2/4009947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2860626223?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony">Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=time-traveler-challenge">time-traveler-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=poc-authors">poc-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=sf-group-2018">sf-group-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=tbr-challenge-2019">tbr-challenge-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=7-kingdoms-challenge">7-kingdoms-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2860626223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7105663307114229653">It’s 2.5 stars rounded down for its ridiculously rushed and unsatisfying last third. Until then, I was mostly along for the ride, willing to forgive its casual sexism and shallow approach to the anxieties of soldiers who face their own imminent demise, because I hoped that Sakurazaka was playing a long game, that he would peel back the layers and reveal a beating heart underneath all the artifice. But no, that didn’t happen. Very disappointing. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2860626223">

<span id="freeTextContainer7686406876816963421">Wow what a rush this book is. From start to finish this book is non-stop. In a world slowly being overrun by monstrous creatures known as Mimics the United Defense Force fights back. This is Groundhog Day meets Starship Troopers with a touch of Mechwarrior. <br/><br/>Keiji Kiriya is new recruit about to enter his first battle only to get killed. Then wake up the previous day. And so the cycle goes and over "time" Keiji learns more about the enemy and how to fight it, especially by watching the world's gre</span>
  <span id="freeText7686406876816963421" style="display:none">Wow what a rush this book is. From start to finish this book is non-stop. In a world slowly being overrun by monstrous creatures known as Mimics the United Defense Force fights back. This is Groundhog Day meets Starship Troopers with a touch of Mechwarrior. <br /><br />Keiji Kiriya is new recruit about to enter his first battle only to get killed. Then wake up the previous day. And so the cycle goes and over "time" Keiji learns more about the enemy and how to fight it, especially by watching the world's greatest soldier, American Rita Vrataski, the Full Metal Bitch.<br /><br />I won't say more about the story as it's not a long book and it's best to find it out yourself. There isn't a dull moment and it leaves you wanting more, but in a good way. Read it before Tom Cruise makes a horrible movie adaptation and makes you wish you'd never heard of it.</span>
